I checked with a local hospital, and they said this recipe is used for overweight patients to get them to lose weight rapidly to prepare for surgery.  I would recommend this recipe to anyone!

text:
First of all, a minor caveat-- I've never had to diet, since I have a pretty fast metabolism, so I can't really compare this to other diets. BUT... Several years ago, I started a new job and found myself sending out for fast food for lunch every day, eating it at my desk. All of a sudden, my clothes started to... *shrink*. I stepped on the scxale and saw that I'd gained 15 pounds!!! I panicked!

Found this "diet" and decided to try it. The weight just went away! It does get a little boring... But it's tasty and painless; think about adding different spices and/or herbs to the soup to vary it... chili powder, curry, etc. Now, I *did* have to change the way I had lunch once I lost the weight... No more fast food breakfasts and lunches (except for the occasional emergency...), trying to get out and walk a bit a few times a week at lunch... But it did get the weight off and-- with my revamped lunch hour-- kept it off.

text:
This is a very good for you and tasty soup, however, when I used to make this some time ago, I also thought that it lacked something or needed a little more flavor.  To give it the flavor it needs, I decided an old trick my grandmother use to use in her vegetable soup.....add a jar or can of sauerkraut in place of some of the cabbage and it gives it just the zing it needs.  Other than that, I left the recipe pretty much as is, I just didn't do a whole lot of measuring, just threw it all together and let it cook.  Enjoy!

I make this when I'm looking to lose weight quickly. I tried to follow the recipe as close as I could, adding minced garlic and omitting the canned green beans, but adding more celery and carrot. (Ew. Am I the only person who can't stand canned green beans?) I also added basil, oregano, thyme and a couple bay leaves. It dosen't affect the fat burning process to add a little flavor, does it? ;) I used my biggest stock pot and it came right up to the edge. So, plan accordingly. TIP: Make sure you are close to a bathroom about an hour or so after you eat this. This cleans out your system VERY well. EDITED: One pot of this soup lasted me one week, eating it three meals a day. To make it more filling, I add just a little cubed chicken breast. Just in a week, I can feel my pants getting looser. Good stuff. ANOTHER TWO WEEKS LATER: Down ten pounds!

text:
The amount of cabbage in this recipe is overpowering. I like cabbage, but this is too much!  If I make this again I will likely only use 1/4 the amount of cabbage and add other healthy veggies like squash and zucchini to make up for it.  I will also cut the recipe in half as it does cook entirely too much... 

The thing that makes this soup a "fat burner" is you can eat ten bowls in one day and still be below 1000 calories. The carbs are low and there is no fat. If you make variations that don't include fat, carbs, and calories than you should still have the "fat burning" effect of this soup.

text:
I add a few different herbs and spices to each batch to give it an international twist. For example, I add chopped cilantro, a little chili powder, and cumin to give it a Southwestern flavor; some oregano, basil, and fresh garlic for an Italian taste; a little curry powder mixed into the cooking soup and chopped fresh mint leaves for garnish on top when serving to give it a unique Moroccan flavor; shrimp or fish boullion, a little soy sauce, and some fresh bean sprouts, minus the tomatoes for an exotic Oriental sensation; chanterelle mushrooms and a pinch of thyme and rosemary minus the tomatoes for a wonderful French taste. All very yummy! Also on the skim milk day add some non-fat plain yogurt to soup.  Also a good tip is to make a banana and milk smoothy on banana and milk day.  All these tips help make my 7 days alot easier.

text:
Hands down this was great, I did take other reviewers suggestions and spiced it up a little, otherwise it would of indeed been bland.  I added: 1 t Chili Powder, 1 t Cumin, 1t Turmeric, 1 t Oregano, 1 t lemon Pepper, 1 t Italian Seasonings, 1/4t chives, 1T Parsley, 1 T Garlic Powder and 2 Bay Leaves.  I also Used v8 Vegetable juice instead of Tomato Juice.  I had to make this in my 20qt Stock Pot because it made so much!  To cut down on time I washed and all veggies and then largely chopped them and threw them into my Food Processor, this took no time at all!  In Minutes I had all the prep done and then threw it all into the pot, added my spice mixture and about 2 1/2 qrts water to cover and let it come to a boil, took about 1 hr, then reduced heat to low and let it simmer on low for about 15 minutes and it was done.  This was so super easy to throw together and there is tons left over!  I will refrigerate half and freeze half.  I did the calculations for calorie, etc and mine came to: Ea 2 c serving has about 62 cal, .12g of fat, 13 carbs, 3 fibers and 3 proteins!  Oh yeah, I used all low sodium stuff, better for the heart! So, we will see if this works to help reduce weight, but I know that one 2 c bowl filled me up so much that I couldnt eat another morsel if I tried!  Low cal and tastes great, this is a winner in my book, hands down! Thank you for posting this recipe!

This soup is really delicious, and easy to adjust to your personal tastes. But just for the record, the soup itself does not make a person lose weight. Eating the low calorie soup in place of a higher calorie food does. It would be very unhealthy for a person to live on this soup alone. The body needs protein and fat to function correctly. So, for a meal I would definitely suggest adding a lean protein, and healthy fat.

As I was lounging with my coffee this morning while browsing this site, feeling sorry for myself for the several pounds I've gained during the Christmas season, I came upon this recipe quite by accident and considered it a hint from heaven! This recipe can, of course, be played with to suit individual tastes, just as I did. First of all, I just basically rummaged the kitchen to use what I had on hand and threw it all in the Crock Pot -- beef broth, V8, a little red wine, Italian seasoning, the dry soup mix (never would have thought of that!), minced garlic, sliced fennel, celery, onion, zucchini and, of course, cabbage. It isn't the best soup I've ever made, but it is good, and certainly an excellent soup if you're watching carbs and calories. Thank you so much for posting the recipe and giving me the inspiration to get my post-holiday diet off to a good start!

text:
I love the taste of this soup which is strange for a meat and potato guy like me.  I've made a few changes.  The first is I add 2-3 15oz cans of chick peas for their protein which is needed to build muscle mass which burns calories more efficiently.  I like tomatoes so I use two 28 oz cans.  Sometimes instead of two cans of tomato juice I'll replace one with spicy V-8 or Sacramento vegetable juice.  I will add a couple of tablespoons of beef base to give a richer flavor.  You don't taste the meat but you do get a heartier flavor.  There's salt in the base but since this is such a large yielding recipe the salt added shouldn't make much of a difference. Lately I've also started adding small cubed beef which I brown first.  Any beef you like is ok, just whatever is on hand. I don't chop the veggies too small and don't cook it as much.  30 minutes is more than enough.  You lose less of the nutrients this way.  Before you start on this recipe there are two things you should be aware of.  It takes a long time to prepare with all the chopping of veggies and, as I said, it's a large recipe.  You're going to need a large stockpot.  Because it does take so long I don't make it as often as I should but I have lost weight with this recipe, enjoyed doing it with such a flavorful recipe and wish everyone else luck achieving the same or better results.  I eat one to two 2cup servings a day and am careful with anything else I eat.  Down 15-20#, another 85 to go.  This recipe hasn't done it

text:
I learned this recipe, in the 1970's, from Weight Watchers (it was in their cookbook and people on the diet learned about it quickly, at the meetings).  I learned to use V-8, diluted, as a base, and to add Worcestershire sauce, zucchini, and yellow squash, and to use a variety of non-starchy veges.  One thing that made a huge difference for me, is to add a heaping dollup of fat-free cottage cheese to the bowl of hot soup - much more satisfying, and takes the squeak off the veges!

text:
I have used this recipe for years - It is really a wonderful, healthy way to lose weight. The idea behind it, is you have at least one bowl of this soup before each meal (breakfast included!). You are not limited to only three, because the more you eat, the more you will lose (honest, tis really works!) My advice to anyone who wants to try this is that you make the entire recipe(it makes a LOT!) but separate the finished soup into daily portions and freeze. This way, you only reheat each portion once, which helps it retain the flavor. If you cook it too much, it tends to lose alot of its appeal. Also, As long as you stick to the same basic recipe as far as the vegitables are concerned, you can add as many varied spices as you want - I'll cook some wit fresh italian style spices, and some with more spicy creole or mexican spices. yum yum! I lost over 50 pounds with this soup, and never felt hungry!

I have made this numerous times, only changing up a few things. I add already seasoned diced tomatoes. Be wary of using dry onion soup mix because it has added salt which is not good, instead substitute 1/4 cup minced onion, 2 tablespoons low sodium dry instant beef broth and 1/2 teaspoon onion powder.  To make mine soupy, I add 2 cans of tomato bisque soup to mine, about 5 cups of water.  I also add a couple dashes of garlic powder and 1/2 tsp crushed red pepper. Tomatoes are known to help satisfy hunger so you can eat this whenever you feel hungry and it doesn't ruin your diet.  I like the added slight "spice" of the red pepper.  Cabbage-soup-diet.com will give you the details of the 7 day diet and helpful tips to doing the diet the right way.  I am beginning day 3 of the diet and I have lost 5 pounds already.  Mind you...It does warrant having access to a bathroom.  I sure am missing my coffee (with creamer) though.

text:
First, it's worth pointing out as others have that this soup is "fat burning" not because of some magical ingredients that melt away the weight, but because it's so low calorie, that meals like this are basically calorie neutral. 

When it comes to food, everything can be evaluated in 3 categories.
- Is it filling? 
- Does it taste good?
- Is it low in calories?

Foods that are a "yes" in the above 3 are rare. A bowl of raw vegetables is filling and low in calories, but would be a bit bland. A cheesecake is filling and tastes good, but is high in calories.

This soup is the triple threat. Tastes great, very filling, and insanely low in calories. It's so low in calories it would almost be dangerous to only eat this everyday! 

Now on to the soup itself, a couple notes:

Size: As others have mentioned the total made is enormous- I thought my large  stock pot would be enough but had to split it into two. You need one of those huge pots, or two small ones.

Customizing: I decided to make tweaks right off the bat. As written it's probably fine. 

That's the great thing about this soup- you can tweak it however you want. I added worcestershire, A1 sauce, and used diced tomatoes with green chiles. Spices included basil, salt, pepper, garlic and a few others. You can do whatever you want!

And going on from there, don't be afraid to add even low calorie things. Some sliced turkey kielbasa would still have this be an absolutely insanely low calorie dish, but add to the taste.

text:
Ignore the warnings of not changing the ingredients, go ahead! Canned tomato juice is high in sodium so I increase the low sodium beef broth. Often I include fresh or frozen veggies that's on sale at the market. I like to always include zucchini and yellow squash. I amp up the carrots & use a whole bunch of celery. I add veggies to the pot at different intervals because I like 'em on the crunchy side. I often change the seasoning packets to chile , taco or whatever suits my fancy. Stick with this without CHEATING and you'll loose weight.  There is a calender of what to eat on certain days that goes with this diet. You can get unhealthy if just eating this and this alone. You're allowed meats & bananas, for example but on specific days. Google "cabbage soup diet schedule" and follow the plan.

I had totally forgot about this recipe until it showed up here today!  I've been thinking about losing a few pounds so I went out and bought the ingredients.
The only substitutions I made were to use Hot & Spicy V8 in place of the tomato juice, I used canned diced tomatoes with jalepeno's and I added about 1/2 lb of ground turkey and a can of chick peas for protein. enough to nearly cover the veggies. And I simply let them cook down into the juice.  This is SOO good -- much better than the recipe of years past!
I may actually stick to the diet this time!
Thanks!  :-)

I remember this soup from the 80's and recently gave it another try. I made a few changes based on comments here.  I used canned crushed tomatos, added two chopped up poblano peppers, two chopped jalapenos, used frozen french cut green beans instead of canned, added about 1 cup sliced fresh mushrooms for that meat mouth feel and I eliminated the dry onion soup mix.  I cheated and sauteed 1 bunch green onion, tops and all, with 4 cloves garlic in 1T olive oil.  I added 1T chili powder and 2t cumin.  The soup turned out great, very filling but you get hungry again soon.  The whole magic fat burning cabbage soup diet can be found at www.cabbage-soup-diet.com.  It is really a behaviour modification plan disguised as a recipe.  But all the veggies make for healthy eating!  Great soup, highly recommend, with some added spices, which do not add calories!

Do you know how much sodium is in this soup? Dried onion soup mix (2,440 mg of sodium), tomato juice (5,232 mg of sodium),  canned green beans (580 mg of sodium), canned tomatoes (1,440 mg sodium), beef broth (890 mg sodium). That's a total of 10,582 mg of sodium per batch, or 706 mg of sodium per serving. That's almost a half a day's worth of sodium per bowl of soup! Insane.

I've made variations of this many times over the years.  I like to use low-sodium chicken broth or vegetable broth, and I also use either fresh or frozen cut green beans.  I stopped using the dry soup mix a long time ago and just add my own seasonings (salt, pepper, herbs, hot sauce) to taste, but my recent addition of a tbsp. or so of garam masala has made this a new favorite in our house!  We try to have a salad with dinner every night, but when that wears thin, a small bowl of this before dinner is a nice change and a healthy way (especially when you take steps to lower the sodium content) to get in an extra serving or two of veggies with minimal fat and calories.

text:
This is a very tasty soup. I knew from reading the recipe that i'd find it a little bland so I added 4 cloves of garlic, crushed, about a teaspoon of coriander powder, celery salt and basil as well as 6 small chillies chopped with the the seeds. It's turned out delicious! I'm a vegetarian so I also substituted the beef broth for vegetable stock (from bullion). 

Be warned - if you are going to use the stated proportions, you will need a very large pot to get all the ingredients in - it ended up being a lot more than I thought it would be, with the soup coming to the top of my foot and a bit tall stock pot!

The great thing about this recipe is that the soup is versatile, you can add different spices and sauces to it and use different stocks and vegetable juice bases to change the flavor (next time I'm thinking of trying a more curried flavor) and you can either roughly chop the veggies if you want it chunky, finely chop them for some bite or puree it if you prefer a thick liquid soup. I'll definitely be making this again.

text:
As a "diet soup" this would get 5 stars...it works to radically reduce calories and carbs as written, and is filling enough to curb a stubborn appetite.  It would be a rare person who would fail to lose weight replacing just one meal a day with this soup.  I dropped one star for the lack of seasoning.  Not many reviewers raved about this recipe without adding their own tweaks.  My advice would be to make a smaller batch to begin with and tweak until you find a seasoning combination that you really like.  If you don't like the taste, you won't be able to stick with it on a frequent, or daily basis, and so it won't work as a weight control tool.  If you get too much of something, you'll be stuck with a couple gallons of soup you'll quickly tire of. (which is what I did!)  Once you've perfected to your own satisfaction, THEN make the larger batch and freeze some of it.  As with most soups, this is better the second day and beyond. I like the idea of rotating flavors, and my next batch I plan to make "bland" and season it in smaller quantities as I pull them out of the freezer. This way I can keep it more interesting from day to day.

For those of you who are cooking for the gout-stricken, this is VERY gout-friendly, and a good way to help get those desirable veggies into the diet...IF you can keep it interesting enough to be eaten on a regular basis!

I made some changes, started this June 27th, down 6 lbs AFTER stuffing my face for 4th of July! Used V8 juice as recommended by others instead of plain tomato juice, used a head of broccoli instead of celery, used red & orange bell peppers instead of green, had beefy onion soup mix so used that, had the carrots cut into chunks like another reviewer suggested (good call!), and boiled 3 chicken breasts, shredded them and added to the soup. Salt to taste. DELICIOUS! So good my mom tried mine and asked me to make her a batch! It reminded us both of Campbell's Vegetable soup back in the day (no idea if it tastes the same now). I could never eat just this all day every day even though it's tasty. Instead I've been using it as at least one meal replacement. Healthy breakfast, soup for lunch (sometimes with, sometimes without triscuits), generally whatever for dinner. This soup is SO low in calories that even a bad day can end with not going over my calorie goals for the day. I exercise regularly but love to eat so this soup has been a great boost in weight loss. I've NEVER lost weight so fast and I'm not hungry! If I get hungry, I have a bowl of this soup! Very pleased with this recipe.

text:
I made this soup many years ago and I was so thrilled to find the recipe again here on allrecipes.com (of course!). Before I share this tip, I must say that although I read many of the reviews, I did not read all 508 of them, so this may have already been shared.

I was at a loss for 2 qts of tomato juice! As I was scouring my pantries for the juice or V8, I found my (very fav!!) Mr & Mrs T Bloody Mary Mix. Knowing it would be all kinds of wrong, I decided to compare the Nutrition Facts to my small amount of Campbell's tomato juice anyway.

Well!!!  Kudos to Mr & Mrs T !!!!

The Nutrition Facts are EXACTLY the same except for a couple of (minor) things.  The tomato juice has 5 grams of sugars and the Mr & Mrs T only has 4 grams of sugars!! Yes, I also know that Mr & Mrs T list high fructose corn sugar as an ingredient that the tomato juice does not have, but obviously it does not affect the Carbs or Sugars!

Ok, there is a tradeoff (of course..lol!) the Mr & Mrs T mix has 650 mg of Sodium, compared to Campbell's Tomato Juice from Concentrate's 470 mgs. But you know the old trick - peel & quarter a couple of potatoes, throw them in to absorb the sodium and then toss them when your soup is done!

So  For all of my fellow Bloody Mary lovers out there, all we need to keep in our pantries is Mr & Mrs T for our cocktails AND any of our recipes calling for tomato juice!

text:
As-is, 4 stars... but so easy to make it 5 if you just add seasoning!  Herbs etc. don't make it less healthy!
I've made this twice now and I love that I can get a huge amount of veggies in at lunch. A few things I've learned while making this:
1) 1/2 head of cabbage is still tons. I'm sure my stock pot wouldn't have fit a whole head.
2) Use only enough water to fully cover the veggies. They will reduce as it cooks.
3) I use two packs of onion soup mix, for personal taste.
4) The herbs I use: Italian mix, oregano, parsley and bay leaves. I also add a fair amount of minced garlic.
5) I thought this would be way too "onion-y", but surprisingly, it's not. 

I don't make this for weight loss... I make this because it's a tasty, healthy soup with lots of veggies!

It is working! I have lost 4 lbs and I'm on day 2 of the cabbage soup diet! I ate the soup because it smelled so good while I was cooking it the night before the diet;  my original plan was to eat this juicy French Dip sandwich my fianc made before having to do this diet, but I just ate the soup. I did have to dr it up quite a bit though. So, that being said, it is OK to dr it up to your liking, TO AN EXTENT. The ingredients aid in your fat-burning, yes, but adding seasoning such as I did, does not ruin the recipe and it just makes you more likely to be successful eating something you can eat Just DON'T add fat if your goal is to lose fat! Here's what I did I added all ingredients to their fullest and DID NOT substitute anything. I used all organic foods Expensive, yea somewhat, but not really when you consider how much it makes and how long you'll have soup for! text:
I am rating this recipe with only one star with a warning; THIS WILL NOT MAKE YOU BURN FAT!  But even though cabbage will not burn fat from your body, it is still ideal for your weight loss diet because it is so low in calories, low sodium and low carbs. It is a great filler for soups to make you feel full.  With this specific recipe, there is not enough nutritional value to make this a good diet soup.  Definitely do NOT add the dried onion soup! It has a tremendous amount of salt which will make you retain water weight.  When I was dieting, cutting out salt alone with no change in my exercise routine, made me lose about 3 pound a week for a month.  So to make this soup great tasting and great for an energy diet meal, add lots of veggies....peas, beans, celery,  etc. DO NOT add tomato juice! Once again, very high in sodium. Add canned tomatoes instead! Sure canned tomatoes have salt but it's minimal and you'll get more flavour and nutrition than the juice.  My secret to this type of soup is a little fresh lemon juice or ReaLemon juice.  Mushrooms are good...spinach is fantastic!  The greener the vegetable you add, the better the nutritional value.  So this soup as written is very, tasteless, counter productive, misleading and wrong!  If you want to make it and like it, that is great if you are aware that it will not "burn" fat or calories and is not a good main diet dish.

text:
I make this soup with these changes and additions: I use fresh green beans, add okra, spinach (for added potassium), barley (for added fiber) and red bell pepper. In addition I use no-salt added Chicken stock and add fresh (when available) herbs and spices such as garlic, parsley, cumin, oregano, etc to taste. I even add either bulk Italian sausage and/or ground turkey breast for taste and to add protein . With the quantity of soup, the meat does not change the nutrition values enough to be a problem. One problem is that no one mentions how large the pot needs to be. The first recipe that I came across said that it made 1 gallon of soup. I had to buy a 10 Qt stock pot to contain it without risking overflowing. When I started adding more veggies and meat I had to buy an even larger stock pot: 16 qt, but I could probably get by with a 12 -14 qt. It is delicious and keeps a long time. I do not eat it exclusively but eat it at least once each day. Does it work? My cardiologist told me that if I could lose 10% of my body weight (214 lbs at that time) that my blood pressure problems would go away. I lost 21 lbs in about six months, went on vacation and ignored all diet restrictions and gained back 10 pounds. Primarily because of this soup I had no problem hitting my 21 lb loss goal by my next cardiologist appointment. Also, my BP fell to well within the normal range. I recommend it for weight loss.

I love this recipe!  Like other reviewers have said, it makes a TON--I halved it right off the bat, and it still made more than I was ready for!  I added some spices--black pepper, garlic powder and a little cayenne.  Also, for those who feel "overwhelmed" by all the cabbage, I'd recommended chopping it more finely, almost diced.  This soup is a fantastic way to get in those veggies during the winter when a salad just doesn't sound appetizing at all!

I like to add a big jar of sauerkraut (not a can) and use low-sodium vegetable juice to give it a little more flavor.  If you like spicy, you could use the spicy vegetable juice.   Update:  I have made this many times now mainly because I like it and it's very low calorie. This soup was my first venture into the dieting world 15 yrs ago.  I need to lose some weight again so I'm making the soup tomorrow.    I have to say though, the diet attached to this soup is pretty nutty.  Although you will indeed lose a surprising amount of weight really quickly eating almost nothing but this soup, it's mostly water weight you will lose and it will really mess up your body, health and metabolism.    *That said*, this is a great diet soup to eat daily to help lose weight if you're including a daily intake of other balanced nutrients.    I regularly do a half banana, mixed berries, ginger, spinach and kale smoothie for breakfast with a little lean protein on the side (approx 300 calories all together).  So now I'm going to try eating healthy small meals like the smoothie 3x a day and eat the soup in between to fill up.  Then every 4-5 days eat slightly more than usual (something high-carb to spike leptin levels) so my body doesn't go into starvation mode, and my metabolism stays charged.   I have 10 lbs to lose in a month so I'll update if this works.  The soup here is slightly different from the classic which I'll list in case anyone is interested:      * 6 large green onions     * 2 green peppers     * 2 cans of tomatoes (diced or whole)     * 1 bunch celery     * 1/2 head cabbage     * 1 package dry onion soup mix     * 1 or 2 cubes bouillon/ stock cubes either chicken or beef (optional)     * Salt, pepper, any seasoning

I made this soup last night so that I could do the diet, but I also had people over so I served it as the first course for dinner. Everyone loved it :) It is very delicious even if you don't plan on eating it all week. I did try some about half an hour before dinner time and thought it was very good but it was missing something--namely a TON of salt but it was still yummy. I went to the cupboard to grab the salt and realized why it was so bland--I forgot to add the onion soup mix! I just threw it in there at the end, stirred well and let it simmer a couple more minutes. I gotta tell you though the soup was still good but I liked it better without the mix. Next time I will skip the mix and just add plain salt. As far as the diet goes, it's my first full day and I've been peeing A LOT, so make sure you do it at a convenient time not a day you have a lot of meetings or anything. And also although volume-wise Ive eaten more than I usually would I am still hungry so if you plan on doing the diet make sure you have a lot of fruits and veggies to supplement on the appropriate days. Good luck to all with your weight loss and if your just looking for a yummy soup go ahead and give this one a try its very tasty!! (although you should only make  of the recipe as it does make A LOT, I used a 14qt pot and there was only a tiny bit of room at the top)

text:
I have made this more times that you could count, because I was making this back in the mid 1970's...it's delicious and I did lose weight on it. I was working retail at the time and the recipe went  through all departments in several of our stores. 
It is a healthy soup and I still make this frequently. I recommend that you prepare it according to  the directions. The weight loss is dependent on the exact ingredients as printed here.  When you begin to add to or subtract from...it upsets the effectiveness of it due to the items you add such as meat or remove, perhaps you don't like one of the veggies, you're playing with the nutritional aspect.

However, if you are NOT interested in the weight loss aspect, then feel free to add meats or seafood...weight loss or no, it's delicious!

text:
I just finished a giant bowl of this Cabbage Fat-Burning Soup.
The recipe rendered u about 24 12 oz servings that I containerized and put in the freezer.
I feel that it needs a few spices to perk it up some but I'll do that as I defrost and eat the remaining servings.
I tried a few spices on my first bowl and that helped.
If you don't have bunches of excess freezer space I'd suggest that you make a half recipe.
I think this soup will improve with age and each batch will probably be more tasty than the last. I know my Celery Soups get better after sitting in the fridge long enough to defrost.
I eat a lot of soup recently and have found that most soup reduce down to VEGGIE smoothies quite nicely with a blender. Turning soup into smoothies improves the portability for on the go consumption.

text:
Yummy soup for this time of year.  This recipe makes lots, had to use two large pots.  My changes to the recipe are as follows:  1)   I exchanged out the tomato juice for spicy vegetable juice.  2) I used 2 cans of Beef Broth (1 in each pot).   3) I used 2 packs of onion soup mix (1 in each pot).  4) I used 2 cans of green beans (1 in each pot).   The rest of the ingredients I split down the middle.  The cooking time went well over the suggested 45 mins.   Turned out just perfect if you like things just a bit spicy, if not stick with the plain tomato juice or vegetable juice.

text:
This make a HUGE pot of soup! It is delicious and I wish mine had more cabbage in it - the biggest head I could find was still on the small side. I used fresh green beans and doubled the beef broth, added Worcestershire sauce, black pepper, hot sauce and pepper flakes - I like flavor. I made another pot and changed the veggies slightly to include cauliflower which I had on hand and saved a copy on here. I add turkey meatballs for meal replacements. This will be my new winter work lunch, it will allow me to save money and lose weight, win-win!  If you decide to change the vegetables around and want to preserve the weight loss property, be very aware to avoid any starchy vegetables and limit vegetables that are high in sugar. I cooked mine about an hour, anymore than that and veggies will be too soft as they keep cooking until they cool and may cook a bit again when you warm up the soup.

I liked this soup a lot, and it didn't leave me feeling hungry. I split this recipe and made it for six servings instead of 15. I only used half a head of cabbage and added extra veggies, including chopped tomatoes, a can of garbanzo beans for protein, and the whole can of green beans. I used half water/ half chicken broth for the liquid to add flavor. I also seasoned with plenty of cracked pepper and garlic powder and it added a nice taste to the broth as well. I didn't have any onion soup mix, so I added a beef boullion cube and minced dried onions as a replacement. In a couple of servings I've heated through with a polish sausage added in, and it makes a very nice addition to the soup. I will make this again!
UPDATE: Try adding italian seasoning to the soup while it simmers. It gave the PERFECT flavor, just the touch I was looking for! It's a 5 star recipe with that one change.

I added a medium size zucchini and used sweet onions, also added, 1 tbsp. parsley, 1 tbsp. oregano, 1 tbsp. basil, 1 tbsp. garlic powder, 1 tsp  cumin and 1 tsp black pepper.  It really made it taste great and nothing else was needed. It also freezes great.  Thank you for this great recipe.

text:
Ive been making this soup for YEARS now. Here are some tips Ive picked up along the way:

Use one large can of diced tomatoes and one large can of crushed. It makes a meatier stew without having those large random pieces of tomatoes that youll inevitable cut up. Absolutely add in a ton of spices and garlic along with the onion mixIll  add in everything from cilantro, paprika, Italian seasoning, bay leaves and/or cayenne pepper! Add in a diced jalapeo or two for a kick. After trial and error, this soup is best made on the stove top rather than trying to make it in a slow cooker. It takes about 2-3 hours to really cook so the carrots and celery are fully cooked. This soup tastes AMAZING the days after you make it and the flavors melt together. It also keeps for a long time as its mostly veggies and beef broth can keep for up to a week. And finally.... this soup will definitely give you gas so just a heads up lol.

text:
I love this soup!  I made a few changes to the recipe because I'm a picky eater and lazy cook.  I hate green beens so I left it out and just placed a little more cabbage and bell peppers in place of it and added some ground black pepper.  Also, instead of regular tomato juice, I used a big bottle of low sodium V8 vegetable juice and instead of a can of beef broth, I used 1 teaspoon of Organic Better than Boullion beef base which you can purchase at Costco and a can of water.  I know this soup would have been just as good without the substitutions.  I ate a bowl as-is then added some tobasco sauce to my second bowl.  Both ways are delicious.  If you're not eating this as a diet soup, you can add chunks of beef, macaroni, pasta, or cheese to make this a meal for everyone and anyone.

I altered the recipe. I added carrots and string beans. I also add parsley, oregano, thyme (just a little bit) and added black pepper, more  than the ingredients stated, to give the soup a little afterward kick. It sneaks up on you after eating the scoop of soup. Also I added chicken stock and lemon juice to cut the tomato taste. Im not a huge fan of the strong tomato taste. If you  do like that strong tomato taste, dont add the stock or lemon. If you are not fan either then try it my way. Pour a little each time to test how it taste. I cant give you a measurement. Its what your taste buds like. I hope you like my additions.

text:
I did NOT make this to lose weight; I just clicked on it because I had cabbage on hand, and made it because I had all the ingredients. It is delicious! I used low sodium V8 and low sodium beef broth. My husband and I both love it. He's been eating it for lunch every day for a week and isn't sick of it yet - he actually comments daily how good it is! We like a lot of spices and flavor so I didn't expect us to enjoy this, but it really is tasty without any added spices. Note this does make a LOT of soup. It filled my soup pot to the brim. (Reminder to those as silly as me, it will rise a little as it heats so make sure you're not at the brim to start - mine didn't overflow but I had to watch it closer than I wanted to.) I simmered for 20-30 minutes then left it warming on low, due to the precarious overflow possibility, for probably 2-2.5 hours (much longer than I thought I would need to, but I was distracted with a newborn and house guests) and it was perfectly done. I tried pureing a portion and adding it back in for a creamier broth as another reviewer suggested, but my husband and I both thought it was better in its original form. Final note, as expected, this does NOT fill you up for a long time, so if you're not looking to lose weight, it is delicious and nutritious as a side to a hefty sandwich. ;)

I made this according to the recipe, but halved all the ingredients, as I couldn't imagine having that much soup! I thought it turned out very well and was quite tasty prepared as described. I also followed one of the other reviewer's suggestion regarding adding ground turkey to provide a little protein to the base. After the soup was done, I bottled and froze in smaller portions, and then prior to heating up each portion, I braise a small portion of ground turkey with cumin, and then add the cooked turkey to the soup and simmer for a few minutes to mix in the flavor.  Delicious and surprisingly filling.

I am a dedicated carnivore so I didn't expect much in flavor out of this.  I was surprised when I made it.  This is really good.  It makes a ton of soup, but it freezes well, so have room in your freezer.  I made it as written, and also have substituted "Wow! I could have had a spicy vegetable juice" for the water.  You can add squash, sweet potatoes, or really any veggies you want, but staying away from white potatoes or corn would be a good idea if you want to loose weight.  I also like to add sliced hot peppers, black pepper and some Stevia for sweetness.  I love sweet / spicy.  This is way better than it sounds.  You don't have to go on some extreme eat this all day diet, just try replacing one meal per day, or even just the snacks with this to help lose a few lbs.

text:
This stuff's not bad!  I thought it would be kind of an annoying veggie-fest but basically tastes like a good vegetable soup.  I happen to like the amount of the cabbage in the soup, and it softens up a lot and loses that... "cabbage" taste, so I found the amount tolerable.  If you like less, use a cabbage smaller than a bowling ball and chop it up in smaller pieces, should be good.  Great for losing swelling if you're trying to avoid salt too, but it does tend to be pretty bland if you use low sodium everything.  I found that stirring in a 1/2 tsp of better-than-beef bouillon was perfect.  I also added 2 lbs of ground turkey (not the stuff from the store - the kind straight from the farm to a local drop point that you buy in bulk, it's more like a turkey thrown through a fan than the mush you get in the tubes).  I found the turkey gave it the protein it's lacking as-is.  Oh also 6-8 cloves of garlic doesn't hurt anything =D  And garlic's good for you too.

Oh btw, the weight loss you get from this is just water weight.  It has almost no carbs, and for every one gram of carbohydrate stored in the body (as glycogen) there is approximately 2-3 grams of water retained.  You lose the stored carbs VERY quickly (and hence, the water weight) if this is all you eat, but it'll come back once you get carbs back in there.  Try going keto if you want to keep that effect going *and lose real fat.

Delicious,flavorful and filling!! If not using for weight loss, this is an easy way to get those 3-5 servings of veggies a day!  I added some frozen peas (gotta love the extra protein!) and about 1 tbsp of freshly minced garlic (great for detox). Also, I used about 10 fresh green beans instead of canned. This makes the soup much fresher-tasting. For those saying it was bland, I used Campbell's tomato juice (can you say lycopene?!) and only added water  when I could see my veggies sticking out of the top while simmering. I also added turmeric (an amazing anti-inflammatory spice), black pepper (to enhance the absorption of turmeric), basil, parsley, and onion powder. Adding kale would be a great addition to the soup. I loved the deep tomato taste and the crunch of the cabbage. Thanks for the recipe! I will be making this often!

text:
This is an amazingly filling and most delicious meal in itself!!! CAUTION: I had to transfer the full recipe into my X-Large canning pot because there was SO much! I'm grateful though, because:  a) it's scrumptious and b) I have a Food Saver and now have a bunch frozen for quick and easy week-night dinners!
I added sauteed mushrooms and spinach and it made a huge flavor difference for us without adding calories! I sauteed the mushrooms and spinach in butter, (well, technically, Smart Balance Organic) and garlic before adding into the soup. That adds just a smidgen more of the gourmet flavor for us. The only other possible alternate I would make is using the Cut Stewed Italian Tomatoes. Just a personal preference as I don't prefer whole stewed tomatoes...but that's just my preference.
I would advise if you make the entire batch, allow extra cooking time. Ours "simmered" for a few hours before the cabbage and carrots were softer to taste. But all that did was enhance the flavor! In fact, I was twice as good the next day!
Would do it again and again!! I highly recommend this recipe! Bon Apatite!

text:
I wanted something to bring to work for lunch in the winter that was healthy - this is delicious! As written, it made a big stock pot full, which is what I wanted. I let it cool off, then put about a cup or so in small freezer ziplock bags and froze them. When I leave for work, I take a bag and let it thaw at my desk - it is pretty much thawed by lunchtime, then reheat it - YUMMY! I only made one slight change and addition: I used V-8 vegetable juice instead of tomato because I don't like straight tomato juice and I added a can of cannellini beans (low cal and good for fiber!). I add a little salt and pepper once it's reheated but that's it .

text:
This is a really delicious soup! The only thing I did differently was at the beginning I used 1 tbsp of oil and sauteed the onion with 2 cloves of minced garlic (I must have my onions sauteed)- once it cooked, I added all the other listed ingredients along with some salt, a tsp of chicken bouillon and 2 bay leaves. Also I only used 1/2 of the tomato juice and doubled the beef broth and then topped off with about 3 cups of water. When I served it, I squeezed fresh lime juice on top. My husband and (usually picky) 11 year old daughter devoured it. We have enough to last us the entire week and to kick start some healthier eating and hopefully some better fitting clothing!

I was looki g for a tecipe similar ro my mom's, but I couldn't find one.  Then I stumbled across this. I thought I'd use it as a rough guide line. 

I had to alter the recipe a bit. I used what I had available as I live in the UK. I used 1 small cabbage (a large would have been too much), 500 ml of passata?, 400 g diced tomatoes, 3 carrots, 2 parsnips,  1 green pepper, 2 stock cubes, amd topped up with water. I threw in my fave herbs (oregano, basil, parsley,  bay leaf,thyme)  I chopped the garlic and added 1/3 onion powder. I didn't add salt as stock cubes have enough salt, but it needed ore salt. 

Second time, I did 5 stock cubes and 2 tins of tomatoes, 1 tsp onion powder, 2 bay leaves and majoram,  no parsley, 5 carrots,  and only topped up the to just go over the cabbage. The rest of the herbs stayed the same and I cut the cabbage smaller and took out the heart.  It tasted miles better this time. 

I've lost weight eating this,  only because it's filling. I don't thi k it has any fat burning properties, just wholesome soup.

Not that this needs another review (= It got cold and rainy and I was craving soup - and this happened across my screen (= Sounded good, and healthy, so . . . (= I sorta halved it . . . I used a nearly 2 quart V8 for the tomato juice. I stirred in the packet of onion soup mix - but left out the beef broth - and a tablespoon of dehydrated garlic. I used 1 can of diced tomato [personal preference], about 2 c carrots, 1 large maui onion, all the celery, a small head of cabbage, the entire can of green beans, and 2 cans of garbanzos [I love them, and one didn't look like much in the pot with the rest of the veggies!] - I also added quite a few baby bellas that I needed to use up. text:
I spray my frying pan with cooking spray and saute my celery, onion and cabbage (sometimes the carrots too) first, to get that roasted flavor a bit first.  I suppose you could also roast them in the oven on a baking sheet sprayed with cooking spray too.  It just adds a bit different flavor to the soup.  I also use V8 instead of tomato juice, and I omit the tomatoes because I do not care for them.  I also don't use the packet of onion soup mix, because there is already sodium in the V8 and the beef broth.  Using low sodium products would be much better, however the soup isn't as tasty without all the sodium so you do need to try and spice it up some with extra herbs.  But all in all, a great soup base recipe.

text:
This is a good BASE recipe for those willing to experiment with different veggies and herbs. I "halfed" this recipe.  I used 3 cloves of garlic (I LOVE garlic lol), 3 carrots, 1 medium onion, 1 (14.5oz) can of no salt added diced tomatoes with juice, 1 head of nappa cabbage (milder in flavor), 1 envelope of soup mix (beef), 2 cans (14.5oz each) of no salt added green beans, 1 jalepeno pepper (diced), 1 quart of low sodium V8, 1 green bell pepper, 1 box (4 cups) of no sodium beef stock, 2 cups of h2o, 2 large sprigs of fresh thyme (be sure to remove the stems after the soup cooks, the leaves will fall right off), 2 TBs of fresh chopped oregano and black pepper to taste. I first sauteed the garlic and veggies in about 1 TB of evoo and then added the remaining ingredients. I let it simmer for about 5 hours until everything was tender. This yielded 15.5 cups of soup for me. I was going to use a couple of bay leaves but I discovered I had none. Tasted great and yielded a low calorie, low sodium (~60 calories per cup and

text:
Memory lane - I remember my mother making this in the 70's.  I made this with some minor modifications based on available ingredients.  I used chicken broth (no onion soup mix or beef broth) and omitted green beans (instead used chopped zucchini).  I started the soup by sweating the onions, carrots and celery in a bit of olive oil with fresh garlic, and then added everything else and simmered until done.  Added some dried basil, a bit of salt and some freshly ground pepper.  This soup is a perfect antidote to holiday overeating.  I haven't made a full diet of it, but I've been having a generous bowl every day this week for lunch and it seems to be tasting better with every passing day.  Lots of vegetable servings here.

text:
This is a great basic vegetable soup recipe.  I made a few changes to enhance the flavor without it being too salty.  Browned the vegetables in a little olive oil as I added them to the pot, adding a pinch or two of salt as they browned.  This really brings out the flavor of the vegies. I don't like canned green beans so I used whole frozen instead.  I used low sodium tomatoes and broth.  Also vegetable juice instead of tomato.  Because the browning released so much flavor, I only used half of the onion soup mix.   Because I made all these changes to make it suit our tastes I rated it 4 stars.

I don't make this with the "fat burning purpose", I make it because it is a great base for many variations.  Here's how I kick it up to a 5 star rating, but remember I make this soup because we like it, not to lose weight.  Because we like a thicker, heartier soup, I start by browning 1 lb of hot italian sausage in my soup pan, then proceed with the recipe as written. I add a couple cloves of pressed garlic and a can of condensed tomato soup.  Let this simmer until almost done (I use very little water-maybe 2 cups), then I add 1 lb of kielbasa (sliced).  Simmer a little longer and you have a meal.  I serve with sesame bread sticks.

I thought this soup was fantastic. In place of the tomato juice, I used the Bloody Mary Mix recipe from this site that I'd had left over from a party and it gave it the perfect kick needed. I can't yet attest to its weight loss properties, but I can say this was a fabulous cold-weather meal and my husband ate two bowls (even though he said he wasn't hungry!).

text:
The key to this recipe is to season the heck out of it and to use the recipe as a base, but modify it to fit your tastes. I didn't use the tomato juice, beef broth or onion soup mix. I added a few cubed potatoes, 6 chicken boullion cubes, a ton of fresh chopped cilantro, red pepper flakes (gave it lots of flavor and kick!), a packet of some Czech soup seasoning, chives, parsley and pepper. It's a filling soup but low in fat, so it serves its purpose well.
I would rate my version a "5" (without seasonings, I can't imagine how anyone could eat this every day), but that's considering what the recipe is intended for. If I rate this without considering it's a diet soup, I'd probably give it a "3".

Yes I made a few changes cuz I had to use what I had on hand. NOTE:  USE A VERY LARGE STOCK PAN. For ALL the tomato products that this recipe called for I used 1 can stewed tomatoes and 1 can diced tomatoes, I used a huge can of cento crushed tomatoes then I filled the cento can with water twice to make sure all the veggies were covered. I used 2 cans of drained green beans instead of one. I ADDED 2 LBS OF BROWNED GROUND VENISON AND 1 POUND OF CHOPPED TURKEY KIELBASA BOTH BROWNED & DRAINED OF ANY FAT. I ADDED A HEAPING TBLSP OF MINCED GARLIC AND A HEAPING TBLSP OF ITALIAN SEASONING AND A FLAT TBLSP OF WET RED CRUSHED PEPPER and a sprinkling of salt and black pepper. I included all the other ingredients that this recipe called for which filled my biggest stock pot to the top and I simmered it on low for probably 45 minutes to an hour. It is so YUMMY, 5 STARS, 2 THUMBS UP AND I'VE BEEN EATING THIS FOR 3 DAYS AND HAVE LOST 4 LBS. I'M SO HAPPY. IT'S ABSOLUTELY DELICIOUS AND I'M LOSING WEIGHT AND HAVEN'T EXERCISED A BIT BECAUSE I'VE GOT THE FLU & PNEUMONIA RIGHT NOW SO THIS RECIPE IS WORKING GREAT FOR ME PERSONALLY TO LOSE POUNDS. BUT I DON'T EAT ANYTHING ELSE. I DO HAVE A VERY GOOD HEARTY SIZED BOWL WHEN I DO EAT THIS every day and as often as I feel hungry every day which is usually twice a day. It very filling and so tasty! Give it a try, you won't be disappointed. Delish!!!!

Made with no alterations at all. Expected it to be bland vegetable soup, ended up with *tasty* vegetable soup. Will add some spices to future iterations just to see what happens, but it really isn't necessary as it's plenty flavorful as-is.

Cooking time should be adjusted closer to an hour, after 25 minutes simmering the soup was barely warm. Increased heat and waited a little longer, and lo and behold there was soup, and it was good.

Everything barely fit in the largest pot we have, luckily the cabbage cooks down a bit . Be prepared to eat soup for DAYS with this recipe! Crack open the tupperware and save for easy reheated meals.

text:
I have made this delicious soup many times and with the guidance of the 7-Day diet, I have seen results! Whether you are preparing for diet or dinner it does get a tad bland so I get creative! First off, I dont understand why they say use canned tomatos and green beans, so I use fresh. I either chop the tomatos or use cherry tomatos. Im not a big fan of green peppers so I use red, yellow, and orange. I switch between regular onions and green onions. I add fresh chopped garlic, fresh chopped jalapeos for some heat, fresh chopped mushrooms, fresh spinach, and fresh bean sprouts for protein. I flavor with fun things out of my spice cabinet such as Rosemary, ground chipotle chile, thyme, basil, etc... gives you a chance to switch up the flavor and keep your pallet interested. Oh! And I let it cook on low all day in the crockpot! Who doesnt love their crockpot?!? Happy cooking!

text:
I love this soup! I don't suggest to change much, but here is what I have learned to do to make it easier. #1 cut the recipe in half, or less.
#2 use a crock pot and cook on low for 5 hours
#3 use fresh green beans, diced canned tomatoes instead of whole, and I use a whole bag of baby carrots instead of chopping, and try for low sodium everything.
#4 season with cayenne pepper. Cayenne is used in many detox diets. It has many health benefits and adds a needed kick to the soup.
#5 freeze perfect portions for quick healthy meals!

text:
My husband and I have been using this soup off and on for weight management.  It works!  We typically lose 20 lbs each in a month on the diet.  (100% Soup day, alternating with vegetables and soup day,  fruit and soup day, lean meat and soup day, banana-dairy and soup day, and so on.  I agree with others that varying the spices is the trick to avoid boredom.  We also eliminate the green beans as we do not care for them in this soup.  Our vet told us to feed canned green beans to our dogs for weight management.  We put 1/2 - 1 can of drained and rinsed green beans in their dry kibble.  They will lose weight and they love the beans.  It also keeps their breath fresh. We give them to our dogs as a treat right out of the can after rinsing off the excess salt.  They love em and they are MUCH cheaper than dog biscuits.  Better for them too!

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
This recipe has a great "base" of ingredients.    I like to tweak and use my own twist when I cook.  I started with  2 small/medium sized cabbages diced up, along with 2 yellow onions, 1 purple onion, 2 green bell peppers, and about 10 stalks of celery.  I sauted these ingredients in a large stock pot in a little olive oil.  I added black pepper, onion powder, garlic powder, celery seed, oregano, and cayenne pepper while the veggies were sauting.  When the veggies started to soften up, I added about 1 tablespoonful of minced garlic and two 14.5 oz cans of fire roasted diced tomatoes.  After cooking this down for a few minutes, I added two 32 oz containers of Swanson Unsalted Beef Broth and two bottles of 46 oz V8 Low Sodium.  I then added sliced carrots, 1 can of reduced sodium black beans, 1 can of reduced sodium garbanzo beans, 1 package of frozen shelled edamame beans, and one  package of Lipton Beefy Onion Soup Mix.  I then added a splash of Balsamic Vinegar and liquid Zatarains  Shrimp & Crab boil for a little zing .... I'm from Louisiana and we like our food spicy!!!  After boiling the soup until the carrots softened up ... I let the soup cool down and added fresh chopped parsley and green onions.  Bon Appetit  and C'est si Bon!!!!  I hope my review helps anyone looking for a twist on this classic recipe !!!!  :-)

text:
BF was looking to drop a few pounds and find a healthy alternative to quick lunches at work since he's often busy enough that he can only find time to go through a fast food drive-thru if I haven't packed his lunch. I used Spicy V8 for the tomato juice. I added in a can of chickpeas to the recipe. I only used about 3/4 of a large head of lettuce so there was still liquid/soup in the end. The recipe had a large yield that I stored in individual freezer bags. This provided both of us with lunches for awhile. He didn't really lose weight from it since I slightly altered the recipe and we weren't just eating this for every meal. I thought it was really tasty though- adding some spices and hot sauce to my individual bowl. Overall, it was a nice alternative to unhealthy fattening foods. Be prepared to have a bathroom nearby the hour or so after you eat this. It's a "cleansing soup."

text:
Yum! This is going to be my go-to veggie soup from now on. I did make a few small tweaks based on others reviews and what I had on hand. I agree that if you are making it for weight loss you should probably keep the recipe as is. As for me, I halved the recipe and made it in my electric pressure cooker. I started with browning some all natural chicken breakfast sausage. I put in most of the veggies, omitting the green beans and peppers but adding frozen okra. I subbed the tomato juice for half a bottle of V8 and the beef broth for chicken. It was so flavorful! There was no need to add any other spices or salt. I decided against using the onion soup mix as I didn't want the somewhat yucky ingredients it can hide. Will definitely use the recipe as a base again, who knows what version it will be next time!

text:
Like many people here, I made it with V-8, using one bottle of high fiber V-8 and one spicy. I followed the rest of the recipe exactly, but oddly, found it rather sweet. I added lemon juice until the sweetness was gone and I was left with only yummy tomatoey spiciness. This is one of those soups that improves as the days go on.  It's hearty and really filling. Also, it took far, far longer to cook than stated. One more thing: don't even attempt to cook this unless you have a very large soup pot. I thought mine was big until I tried to cram everything in! I hardly had enough room to cover all the veggies with water.  Will make again (especially if it leads to weight loss).

text:
I have made this many times using it along with the cabbage soup diet plan. However this is a bit "large," the original soup didn't have carrots or green beans. First, this is a BIG soup, you will need a BIG pot or two. I use a cabbage of about 950 to 1000 grams, no carrots or green beans, but use the onions and celery and on a good day a can of mushrooms. I use V8 juice (lg can) and sometimes use diced tomatoes instead of whole or a combo of the two. I don't add any beef stock but do use either Italian or herbs de province and one or 2 tbls tomato paste and the onion soup mix. I usually simmer for about 2 hours, stirring occasionally, it is good I agree..

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
I happened to buy a lot of cabbage. When I got home  from store I saw this recipe pop up. I've never made this kind of soup before. I read the recipe, and the 4-5 comments that followed. I gathered that there is room to improvise a tad, and that some found it bland. 

So I pulled out my slow cooker (largest pan I could find). Shredded cabbage, celery, carrots, onions. I then added 3/4 of of box of tomato soup I found in my fridge and 1/4 jar of marinara sauce, and I topped it off with 3/4 jar of kimchi (someone recommended sauerkraut, which I didn't have).  I mixed it all, and let it cook. 
I thought the result would go into trash, but to my surprise it turned out great. So great that my husband instead of eating his dinner proceeded to eat two portions of this soup! To add little fat to the soup (since I didn't have broth), I topped it with dollop of mushed avocado! Thanks for great soup!

text:
I love this soup! I make it any time I'm looking for a low calorie, filling meal. This recipe makes two large batches, so be cautious when you're cooking. I usually divide it evenly into two large stock pots. I also brown a package of extra lean ground turkey and add that in for some protein. I've also tried with garbanzo beans, which is also pretty good. For some extra flavor, I add Cajun spice, chili powder, and cayenne pepper - it really takes this dish to a whole 'nother level, but you could play with seasonings as you see fit. It's a very versatile recipe for different seasoning preferences. Happy eating (& dieting!)

text:
I did not make this soup to lose much weight, I recently started a desk job and have found that I put on a few pounds so I thought incorporating this into my regular diet would help sustain my weight as eating out will just make me poor and eventually gain weight.  I made something like this a long time ago and said I would NEVER do it again. I kept this recipe in my favorites and decided I would try this one. This is NOT the same recipe I did years ago or my taste buds have changed. Changes I made: I used grass fed beef bone broth and I am not fond of green bell peppers so I did not use them. I like the hardiness of this soup, I made sure to cut all of my vegetables on the large side so that they would stay whole throughout the week, this worked great.  I will make this recipe more often. As many others have said this makes a lot of soup so that you can eat it as often as you want throughout your day to lose unwanted weight. I add it to my meals 2 times a day I have already lost the few pounds I put on since starting my new job. Now to find time to workout again ;-/
Hope this was a review looking at. Good Luck with your own goals.

Good recipe, makes a big ol' pot!! Now I did add seasoning (oregano, a whole lot of black pepper, and dried jalapeo for some kick) and used chicken broth instead of beef (it's what I had). Don't be afraid to add spices and such. It's not that the soup BURNS fat, it's that it's very low calorie no fat no carb. adding spices won't hurt anything, but if you start adding things that contain more calories (rice, noodles, etc) you'll be adding more calories.

I also used V8 instead of straight tomato juice for extra flavor and nutrients. It's super filling and delicious.

LOVED THIS SOUP!  I did change it up a bit.  I felt one whole head of cabbage was a bit much and since I had a half head of red cabbage  I used that and took the suggestion of another reviewer and added a 16 oz. jar of sauerkraut.  Worked great!  In place of whole tomatoes, used two 15 oz. cans of spiced diced tomatoes  for added flavor.  We had some vacuum sealed turkey from a recent dinner  and I chopped up  about a pound and added it to the pot. I also added three cups of water so I would have plenty of juice.   It took me a whole lot more than twenty minutes to chop all of this up but it was well worth it.  I cooked it for a little over thirty-five minutes.  The veggies were sill crunchy but that did not bother me.  I would much rather have them crunchy than soft.  I have a bowl every noon.

text:
I don't even remember why I googled this soup, but this was the first recipe in the search. Actually, I saw a colleague eating soup for breakfast which I assumed was part of her countdown to wedding eating plan. After seeing the simple the ingredients and the reviews, I had to try it. CAVEAT: I typically try to make recipes as written the first time, unless there are things in the review that are noticed by lots of people or that I know I can't/won't/don't eat or use. For example, I used about 2 handfuls of minced dried onions as I don't care for the texture or taste of raw/cooked onion. Per reviews, I also cut my cabbage in half.  I used my 7.5qt LeCreuset and there's no way it would have held a whole one. I swapped tomato juice for the V8 based on reviews, and I used a carton and a half of beef broth. Everything else I eyeballed: baby carrots, fresh green beans, celery. I don't like huge tomato chunks, so instead of the whole ones, I added 1 can of diced tomatoes with green chiles, and a bag of frozen butternut squash (fridge cleaning). I also added one can of chickpeas for the protein.  Smart move that kicked up the heartiness and the feeling of being full. I just let it simmer for 1.5-2 hours. I used the tenderness of the carrots as a test of doneness. It's pretty tasty! Not too tomatoey.  It would definitely take willpower to eat this multiple times a day, so I recommend pairing it with meat some days or changing the spices to psych yourself into it. Then again, plenty o

This soup was pretty easy to make. I made as directed except for only using one onion (because I thought I had more but I only had one) adding some green onion to compensate for using only one onion, using petite diced tomatoes instead of whole ones, and adding some spice (garlic powder, onion powder, cayenne, celery salt, parsley, bay leaf, and oregano). I thought it tasted okay. I'm not a big soup eater though, so okay is pretty good praise from me. :)  As for the weight loss, I just ate my first bowl tonight so I can't say if it works. I will say that the one bowl was pretty filling, despite being nothing but veggies, so I can see how this would help people who try to lose weight.

I make this soup regularly and I regularly shake up the ingredients.
I have never used the onion soup mix as it is too salty for me. I sometimes put in a jar of  salsa which changes it completely.  Or I may use just chicken broth  with out any tomato based products.  Or I use 2-3 tablespoons of  tomato paste instead of the tomato juice.  I nearly always use  the full head of cabbage because I like the consistency of  a full bodied soup  and I put about 3/4 of it in containers in my freezer.  Defrosting is a breeze in the microwave. I call this  my 'Make it Your Way' soup!

First time I made per recipe- loved it but a little too salty.  So, next time I omitted onion soup mix- then thought I have the trinity of southern cooking (sauteed onion, peppers and celery) so I added Tony Chauceries seasoning- yup, southern flavored soup.  The next time I thought maybe somewhat Mexican so I started as usual and added 6 bay leaves, menudo seasoning, or add oregano, cumin, pepper flakes and then served over tortilla chips with some cheese on top.   Wow- so a great soup base that can be varied many ways.  And no canned green beans, but fresh green beans or cauliflower or broccoli- whatever I have fresh.  Very healthy too!

text:
This is light and healthy. It just needed something to punch up the flavors a bit. I added red pepper flakes(1 tsp for a 3rd of the recipe) and a pinch of salt. Since this soup was intended to help with weight loss I'm sure the omission of sodium was intentional as it makes you retain water but I thought the flavor called for it. It would still be good with just the red pepper though. I also didn't have tomato juice and used mashed tomatoes and water. I increased the beef broth slightly and simmered for much longer than the recipe suggests. Be aware if you're cooking for one that this recipe yields a large amount of soup. I would make this again it's a refreshingly light dish.

I used three small cans of V8 juice and one spicy V8. Since I didn't add the full amount of tomato juice called for, I added almost the entire carton of 32 oz beef broth. Excellent with a biscuit, although that's not helping reduce the fat! :)  Great soup not only on a cold day like today, but anytime. Will get better after it stands, I'm sure.

text:
I made this soup yesterday and cut it to 1/2 the recipe. I'm sure glad I did, since it filled my largest pot. I made it exactly as directed and as it was cooking for at least 1/2 hour it was lacking in taste and the carrots and cabbage weren't nearly done. So I kept cooking it and added some Lawry's Seasoning Salt, a little Italian seasoning, celery salt, garlic powder, Thyme and kept tasting. Still not enough flavor so I added some chili powder and cooked it until the carrots and cabbage were tender (probably an hour and a half) and finally the taste was great. My husband loved it, and I did too with the additional seasonings. Had some again for lunch today and still have enough for more that two more helpings.  It's a keeper with my additions.

text:
This soup is delicious!! I am starting a diet and I'm looking forward to seeing how well this recipe works for me. Just a warning, this recipe makes a LOT of soup, so it's great for feeding a lot of people or for having it many days in a row. If you're just cooking for yourself though and don't want a lot of leftovers, you may want to half the recipe. I filled up two large Tupperware containers with it, and I expect it will last me all week! It's also really cheap to make which is even better. Also, the recipe calls for it to simmer on medium for 20 minutes or so. Because there is a lot, make sure it's heated through and bubbling before you start the timer. I had it on the stove for about 20 minutes before it even started bubbling. It's definitely worth a go!!

If adjusting the recipe, don't add sugar or carbs.  I season with only salt, pepper corns and about 3 - 4 bay leaves.  No V8 or tomato juice, just beef broth, water & a can of tomato sauce.  All other ingredients stay the same, except for more veggies & I add mushrooms.  You will be guaranteed to lose weight.

I make a pot & take containers to work for lunch.  Sometimes I add a splash of vinegar & siracha in my container making it more of a hot and sour, just to change it up a bit.  You can add pork sausage, beef, chicken, etc.  I use beef shank for more flavor.

text:
I will definitely make this again.  Great recipe.  However, it took ages for me to peel and chop all those veggies and then I had to cook the soup an hour more than the time recommended.  My husband  can't tolerate crisp veggies and even then some of the carrots and the cabbage were still crispy.  Next time I will use Savoy cabbage.  I also used only one can of tomatoes.  As suggested by one reviewer I used V8 and the broth was really bright red.  I also added one head of garlic which I sauted with the onions to start.  I think tomatoes can inhibit complete cooking so next time I will try to cook the veggies with the broth first and as little tomato juice as possible.  Then add the rest of the juice and the can of tomatoes.
For my husband I added leftover brown basmati rice and some ground cooked turkey.  Neither of us has a weight problem but we try to eat as healthily as possible.  This recipe would get five stars if I'd had fewer problems, but the taste was fantastic.

I would definitely make this again.  I did make small changes here and there and I know a lot of people don't care for that but there we are.  I used frozen green beans instead of canned.  I thawed them first.  I used a half head of cabbage because as I started chopping it, I realized if I added the whole thing I might not have any room left in the pot!  I used a can of beef broth and a can of beef stock.  I also used a few dashes of Worcestershire which boosted the flavor very well.  This came out great and more importantly, I love it!  I'll be eating it for days and I hope to see the waistline shrink because of it!  OH!  I also used 2 quarts of V8 instead of tomato juice.

I don't make this soup to try and lose weight, so I can tweak it in several ways if I want. The name seems to turn people off, but if I can convince them to try it they always want more!

text:
This is actually a pretty tasty recipe and very low calorie. I can have a heaping bowl for dinner at only 150cal a serving. While replacing dinner with this, I seem to be losing about a pound a week. 

When I make this recipe I do make some changes, I don't include the tomato juice as I have acid reflux. I also skip the peppers, which get mushy in soups, and just double up on green beans. To flavor the soup since I just use more stock instead of tomato juice, I use a tablespoon of Gochujang (Korean hot pepper paste). This gives the stock a good flavor and adds a kick to the recipe. 

If you know you're one of the people who doesn't digest leafy greens without audible evidence, it's not a bad idea to take some Beano or Gas-X before eating this soup.

I know it's asked not to rate a recipe if you make changes but my only changes are that I add garlic (whole cloves) and allow the garlic and onion to simmer for about an hour because I like my onion and garlic mushy. I also use veg juice rather than tomato juice. I add the other vegs (but fresh green beans not canned) afterwards. This freezes well. This will be a staple in my fridge and freezer all winter.

text:
Have made this once so far. Really liked it! I'm not eating it every meal, just for dinner each day, and its been fantastic. Also I only made half the recipe (since i live alone, and also dont want to have to freeze it), and i made mine into 5 servings... so that'd be the equivalent of making 10 servings out of the original recipe. 

Only modification I made was that I used vegetable broth instead of beef broth (already had vegetable broth i needed to use up in the fridge), and because of that change I got "beefy onion" soup powder at the store instead of the regular onion. I also added 1/2 lb ground turkey to mine (would be 1lb per full batch).

I definitely plan to make this again... I think the only changes I would make are adding some mushrooms, a little garlic, and possibly adding some tomato paste or blending some of my ingredients to make it creamier. Great as is too though!

TASTY! I added an 8 oz jar of rich salsa and cilantro. It came out with too much tomato flavor where you couldn't taste the other veggies I added (snap peas w/ pods, broccoli, cauliflower, bell pepper and at the last second - per bowl: baby spinach). THAT turned out very good.  Also, take a look at the "Ginger Beef" recipe (Allrecipes). The flavors in the two recipes are quite similar, so you might explore using this soup as base, and adding the Ginger Beef portion as a variety.

text:
I love this soup. It's a very forgiving a recipe.  Since it's harvest time, I was trying to use up a lot of vegetables.  One of the best additions was adding greens.  I used Swiss Chard adding the chopped white stems with the potatoes at the beginning and the leaves with kale   later in the cooking. I also used canned Tomatoes & Chilies which gave a little kick to the soup. From the garden I also added zucchini, yellow squash, green beans and parsley.   I used the Onion Soup Mix, but used my own vegetable broth made from all the peeling, onion skins, etc I keep in the freezer until the bag is full. Works well with V8 juice or tomato juice or a combination of the two.   This is soup is also great to use with some of the large outer leaves of cabbage which frequently get tossed out.

text:
This is pretty good, but I wasn't as impressed as I was expecting to be.  I used the Hot & Spicy V8 and cut the celery (I don't like it) and it was still a little bland (as other reviews said), so I added a 2nd packet of onion soup mix, some cayenne and a dash of salt.  That helped a little, but I think that next time I will just nix the onion soup mix and add a good amount of Tony Chachere's creole seasoning and some cayenne for a nice kick!  Very filling, though and makes enough to feed an army!
